<!-- ===================== Host: Teddy Kelvin ===================== -->

### Topic: topic-cryptocurrencies

Title: Cryptocurrencies
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any: https://picsum.photos/seed/spt-crypto/800/400

Body:

I'm currently working on building a new decentralised trading engine for spot and perpetual futures focused on **fairness**. This touches on an intersection of a few topics:

### What this touches

- **finance**: central limit order books, [frequent batch auctions](https://academic.oup.com/qje/article/130/4/1547/1916146), automated market makers, derivatives
- **computer science**: distributed systems, databases, computer security
- **mathematics**: cryptography, probabilities, game theory, mechanism design

### How the session would run

1. A from-zero primer on how exchanges actually work — *no prior crypto knowledge assumed*
2. Where fairness breaks down today (front-running, MEV, latency games)
3. Hands-on: we sketch a fairer matching mechanism together and argue about it

I'm comfortable with the computer science part due to my background but only in the last couple years I've become comfortable with the financial part, as part of this project. I'm learning and discovering new things constantly. It's *very* exciting! Skim the [Ethereum whitepaper](https://ethereum.org/en/whitepaper/) beforehand if you want a head start, but it isn't required.

### Topic: topic-knowledge-infrastructure

Title: Knowledge Infrastructure
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

There is a significant part of the scientific community who feels concerned about the future of science infrastructure.

### What counts as science infrastructure

1. Science institutions — universities, research organisations, companies
2. Research facilities — labs, offices, buildings, equipment
3. Talent — people
4. Communication — conferences, journals, papers, peer review
5. Funding — grants, grant proposal writing, government funding

**Knowledge infrastructure is about the communication part.**

### Why it matters

This is not about abstractly promoting communication and collaboration. This is about an absolutely vital and core component of how science works: unless we communicate effectively what knowledge we have discovered, we are bound to re-discover it. Maybe it's ok? Some inefficiency always exists. *No!* This is not about inefficiency: if we can't utilise what exists, we'll never be able to build on top of what others discover. Isolated discoveries mean no knowledge accumulation which leads to the breakdown of the global science machinery.

Look at [arXiv](https://arxiv.org) and [PLOS](https://plos.org) as existence proofs that the machinery can be rebuilt differently. Many paths and approaches to fix this, open to discussion.

### Topic: topic-digital-protocols

Title: Digital Protocols
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I'm very familiar with digital protocols, especially in the domain of decentralised networks and distributed systems. I think the most relevant today and for this course are ATProto and ActivityPub, with the reason being that they give good answers to questions such as data ownership and data sovereignty. I love talking about these, or more traditional/fundamental protocols (such as HTTP, SMTP, etc), or other brand new or existing ones (such as iroh and okTurtles Chelonia).

### Topic: topic-ai

Title: AI
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any: https://picsum.photos/seed/spt-ai/800/400

Body:

I'm fascinated with the AI advancements of the post-ChatGPT world. The world of software engineering is **completely revolutionised** because of these innovations. Open source has been transcended. I'm excited about these new tools and use them as core tools for my work albeit, indeed, the future is generally *substantially unclear*.

### Three threads I can pull on

1. **Open weights models** — the Chinese ecosystem (DeepSeek, Kimi, MiniMax, GLM) as the only meaningful counterweight to a centralized AI future dominated by the three main corporate players (OpenAI, Anthropic, Google)
2. **Local inference** — running capable models on your own hardware with [llama.cpp](https://github.com/ggml-org/llama.cpp), [Ollama](https://ollama.com), LM Studio and friends, and why that matters politically, not just technically
3. **What changes for making things** — how a small civic-tech team's cost structure looks when software mostly writes itself

### What I'll leave to others

I'm also interested in discussing the dangers of AI which are unprecedented on multiple levels and dimensions. I won't expand on them in this section, not because they are not enormously significant, but because I feel they are better represented in this institution by others.

A lot of this knowledge is now obsolete due to AI agents but high-level understanding and expertise on system design, product design, and architecture remain crucial – maybe even more so than before.

### Topic: topic-encrypted-communications

Title: Encrypted Communications
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Encrypted communications is a fascinating topic in human history. With the advent of PGP in 1991 and more importantly Signal app (as Open Whisper Systems when it came out in 2013) we acquired an extremely powerful tool: provably secure and instant communications available at scale.

Western governments attempt to ban these tools every couple of years. Whether that's correct or ethical is an open question and something we can debate but the tools' importance cannot be understated with the reason being such tools can enable unprecedented coordination and power for small groups of people across the whole world.

### Topic: topic-digital-deliberative-spaces

Title: Digital Deliberative Spaces
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

People collectively thinking, discussing, and deciding what they think about an issue is an important aspect of quasidemocratic polities. Ideally, deliberation enables **peaceful synthesis of conflicting preferences and needs**. Local assemblies are a *simple yet dangerous* tool to do this. They are simple because it's just people gathering; they are dangerous because unless there is appropriate structure to them, chaos is likely.

### Research these before starting

1. [Polis](https://pol.is) by The Computational Democracy Project
2. [Community Notes](https://communitynotes.x.com/guide/en/about/introduction) by Twitter
3. [vTaiwan](https://info.vtaiwan.tw)'s open consultation platform

### Read this book

1. *Open Democracy*, Hélène Landemore, 2020

See how others do it: there are a number of organisations in the UK that are working on citizen assemblies and participatory democracy. There is a lot of space for more, both in person but also digitally. Research, experimentation, and plurality are important to help make assemblies higher quality and hopefully more meaningfully useful in today's British society.

### Topic: topic-learning-intentional-communities

Title: Learning Intentional Communities
Host: host-teddy
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-10
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Universities around the Western world are becoming less relevant. Anybody can learn anything online on their own. Yet learning communities remain crucial. They facilitate people meeting, inspiring, supporting each other. Residential communities are a great way to approach this. You are in one this year. Let's start 20 more like it!

Research these related topics:

1. Fractal NYC and the Fractal Campus course
2. Chautauqua
3. Radical Routes
4. Feÿtopia
5. Mondragon University

<!-- ===================== Host: Hayley O'Brien ===================== -->

### Topic: topic-ai-in-campaigning-2026

Title: AI in Campaigning in 2026
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I can help fellows think beyond *"how do we use AI?"* to *"what changes because AI exists?"* My work sits at the intersection of organising, campaigning and emerging technology: testing where AI **actually improves** political work and where it creates new risks. Through [Campaign Lab](https://www.campaignlab.uk) I've worked with technologists and supported experiments ranging from campaign training simulations to hyperlocal chat interfaces, social listening innovations and agentic experiments, with a focus on keeping humans in the loop rather than replacing political judgement. I have some experience of training campaigners in using AI tools and also creating organisational policies.

### Questions I'm useful for

1. What campaign functions should be automated — and which never should be?
2. How do you run **ethical** political experiments?
3. How do you test tools safely in real environments?

I'm interested in political products that increase *participation, responsiveness and capacity* rather than simply optimising persuasion. I also increasingly have a watching brief on how the capacities can be used for more problematic ends.

### Topic: topic-hyperlocal-politics

Title: Hyperlocal Politics
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I've spent a lot of time trying to understand what politics looks like when you stop starting from Westminster and start from people's everyday lives. Through Campaign Lab research we've looked at local digital spaces, community conversations and the way issues emerge and travel locally.

I can help fellows think about questions like: How do people experience politics outside election periods? How do local identities shape issue salience? How do you design interventions that feel genuinely local rather than nationally templated? I'm particularly interested in translating community insight into campaign strategy: how listening becomes action and then communication back to communities.

### Topic: topic-running-experiments-uk-campaigns

Title: Running Experiments in UK Electoral and Campaign Contexts
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Most political innovation dies because people either over-build or never test. A lot of my work has been about creating practical ways to experiment inside campaigns and institutions with limited time, money and appetite for risk.

I can help fellows design political experiments: choosing hypotheses, defining success, running pilots, evaluating outcomes and deciding whether something should scale. This includes campaign messaging tests, organising interventions, behavioural experiments, tool adoption and operational workflow changes. I'm particularly interested in helping people build evidence rather than anecdotes and in adapting experimentation methods to the constraints of UK politics.

### Topic: topic-mps-offices

Title: MPs' Offices: How Representation Actually Happens
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

One of the more unusual areas I can support on is understanding MPs' offices as organisations. Through our research and practical work we've looked at how MPs' offices actually function — workflows, staffing, onboarding, technology, leadership, casework, decision making and institutional constraints.

I can help fellows understand questions like: What is an MP's office optimised for? Why do good ideas fail to get adopted? How does constituency representation really work? What are the bottlenecks? I've run design sprints and practical sessions looking at how offices operate and what better infrastructure could look like. This is especially useful for anyone interested in democracy, public institutions, civic products or state capacity.

### Topic: topic-designing-campaign-tools

Title: Designing Campaign Tools
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of civic and political technology fails because it solves an imagined problem rather than a real one. Through Campaign Lab and product experimentation I've spent years thinking about how political tools get adopted — and why they usually don't.

I can help fellows move from idea → user → workflow → adoption → scale. That includes discovery, prototyping, testing in live environments and designing for exhausted campaigners rather than ideal users. I'm particularly interested in questions like: Why do organisers abandon tools? How do products fit into existing workflows? When should you build versus adapt? How do you know if a product is creating political value?

### Topic: topic-parties-lobbying-power-uk

Title: How Political Parties, Lobbying and Power Work in the UK
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of people understand UK politics formally but not operationally. I can help fellows understand where decisions actually get made: the relationship between parties, MPs, special advisers, local government, campaigns, funders, members, parliamentary structures and informal networks.

My background includes working in parliament, running Labour Together, convening election review processes and spending years operating between campaigns, think tanks and politicians. That means I can help translate abstract questions ("How do you influence Labour?" "Who matters?" "What does Parliament actually do?") into practical strategy. I've run sessions on navigating UK political systems, identifying pressure points and understanding the difference between formal constitutional power and real-world political leverage.

One of the things I spend a lot of time helping people with is moving from "this is unfair" to "this is changeable". I can help fellows map systems and identify leverage: who controls implementation, who shapes narratives, where informal veto points exist, where legitimacy matters, and where small interventions create outsized effects. I'm particularly interested in helping people understand that lobbying is rarely just meetings — it's often about creating conditions where a decision becomes easier to take.

### Topic: topic-mechanics-of-political-attention

Title: The Mechanics of Political Attention
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Political communication increasingly isn't just about having the strongest message — it's about understanding how information moves. I'm interested in the relationship between **message, messenger, medium and distribution**: why some political ideas spread while others disappear, why the same message lands differently depending on who delivers it, and how platforms shape what people see, trust and act on.

Through my work across campaigns, organising, experimentation and political technology, I've explored how political attention forms in practice — from local Facebook groups and messaging apps to campaign content, community networks and conversational spaces. I'm particularly interested in moving beyond broadcast models of politics towards understanding politics as something relational and distributed — built through networks, conversations, repeated interactions and trusted messengers rather than centralised communication alone.

### Topic: topic-constructing-legitimacy

Title: Constructing Legitimacy
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of political and organisational problems are not really persuasion problems — they're legitimacy problems. People often know what needs to happen but disagree on who gets to decide, whether the process was fair, or whether they trust the people leading it. I'm interested in how legitimacy gets constructed in practice: through participation, transparency, shared ownership, evidence and creating processes people recognise as fair.

I can help fellows think about questions like: How do you make decisions people will actually follow? How do you create buy-in without formal power? How do you design participation that is meaningful rather than performative? How do you create legitimacy for new technologies or organisational change?

### Topic: topic-bridgebuilding-political-conflict

Title: Bridgebuilding and Navigating Political Conflict
Host: host-hayley
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-12
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of my work sits at the boundary between communities that often misunderstand each other: technologists and campaigners, researchers and practitioners, institutions and communities, organisers and policymakers, central and local actors.

I can help fellows think about how to translate between different incentives, vocabularies and ways of working. Political work inevitably involves conflict — between values, strategies, personalities, incentives and limited resources. I'm interested less in eliminating conflict and more in using it productively: When is disagreement useful? How do you stop groups fragmenting? How do you navigate coalition tensions? How do you build consensus without flattening differences?

### Topic: topic-iad-framework-ostrom

Title: The Institutional Analysis and Development Framework of Elinor Ostrom et al.
Host: host-sam
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-14
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

- 'Self-governance is possible' ('beyond "tragedy of the commons"')
- The value of 'cheap talk'
- Trust and reciprocity
- Principles for governing common-pool resources
- Norms and rules: Crawford and Ostrom's 'grammar of institutions'
- Modeling action situations
- Operational, collective choice, and (meta-)constitutional situations
- Polycentric governance: when and how action situations interlink
- Social-ecological systems
- Institution and infrastructure: application to 'sociotechnical systems'
- What happens when institutional actions are automated?

### Topic: topic-web-data

Title: Web Data
Host: host-harvey
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

While in theory we can gather the internet we need from the open web, in most cases we are constrained by the compute resources we have access to. One way round this is looking at some of the aggregated resources available and looking at how we can use these and apply them to our problem. I'll go through some of the large publicly available resources that it is worth being aware of, looking at how we access them, and some worked examples of using them in real projects, in particular how we can combine different datasets to unlock answers to a problem we're trying to solve.

### Topic: topic-structured-data-extraction

Title: Structured Data Extraction
Host: host-harvey
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Getting useful data out of the internet often requires processing raw text and turning it into something usable. I can help explain how modern AI tooling makes this possible, how to use a standardised interface to extract structured data using either larger model providers or open source alternatives.

### Topic: topic-training-and-serving-local-ai-models

Title: Training and Serving Local AI Models
Host: host-harvey
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Using the frontier models of the major AI labs can make projects prohibitively expensive. Fortunately many projects do not in fact require their capabilities and we can replace them with much smaller open source models trained on affordable local hardware or cloud compute. I can help if you're looking to find ways to make projects which incorporate AI models more sustainable by using open source models.

### Topic: topic-data-pipelines

Title: Data Pipelines
Host: host-harvey
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Projects using AI as part of a process are often broken down into stages in order to analyse the behaviour of complex and non-deterministic elements of a program, as well as to allow it to be distributed across different hardware. I have experience working with building these pipelines and can advise on development.

### Topic: topic-science-of-collectivity

Title: The Science of Collectivity
Host: host-zara
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

This foundational lecture explores how groups of humans can exhibit emergent behaviors and intelligence that transcend what any individual could achieve alone. Drawing from neuroscience, complexity science, and social psychology, we'll examine the mechanisms that enable collective action and decision-making. We will cover:

- Why the collective? Going beyond the individual brain
- Emergence in social systems: the scientific principles behind how simple interactions between individuals give rise to complex collective behaviors — from flocking patterns to social movements
- Collective Intelligence: when and why groups outperform individuals, exploring the conditions that foster collective problem-solving versus groupthink and social contagion
- Social Technologies as Cognitive Extensions: how tools, rituals, institutions, and digital platforms extend our collective cognitive capacity and enable coordination at scale

Key Question: What transforms a collection of individuals into a genuinely collective intelligence capable of solving problems no individual could tackle alone?

### Topic: topic-experimental-governance-in-the-wild

Title: Experimental Governance in the Wild
Host: host-zara
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

This topic explores real-world experiments in social innovation. We will discuss prefiguration, transfer cultures, communes, and examples of social experimentation.

### Topic: topic-commoning-theory-and-praxis

Title: Commoning: Theory & Praxis behind Experimental Spaces
Host: host-zara
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

> "In facing up to the many profound crises of our time, we face a conundrum that has no easy resolution: how are we to imagine and build a radically different system while living within the constraints of an incumbent system that aggressively resists transformational change? 'Commoning' refers to acts of mutual support, conflict, negotiation, communication and experimentation that are needed to create systems to manage shared resources. This process blends production, governance, culture, and personal interests into one integrated system." — David Bollier

This topic explores commoning as both practice and political technology for collective resource management.

### Topic: topic-future-crafting

Title: Future Crafting
Host: host-zara
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

This topic covers issues of prediction, risk management and forecasting and how these tactics influence the future. There is a difference between predicting what is likely given where we are now and the current conditions, compared to creating possibility. All too often futurism conflates these two. We'll explore methodologies for collective visioning and the political technologies of future-making.

Optional Reading:

- *The City of Tomorrow: Sensors, Networks, Hackers, and the Future of Urban Life*, Carlo Ratti & Matthew Claudel
- *Hegemony Now: How Big Tech and Wall Street Won the World (And How We Win it Back)*, Jeremy Gilbert & Alex Williams

### Topic: topic-separatist-utopias

Title: Separatist Utopias
Host: host-zara
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

In this discussion group we will explore how collectives form boundaries and maintain coherence. We will examine the political technologies of inclusion/exclusion and the science behind group identity formation. When do groups benefit from separation vs. engagement with larger systems?

Key optional readings:

- Hirschman, Albert O. "Exit, voice, and the state." *World Politics* 31, no. 1 (1978): 90-107
- Introduction from Ruti, Mari. *The Ethics of Opting Out: Queer Theory's Defiant Subjects*
- B.F. Skinner — *Walden Two*

### Topic: topic-utopian-family

Title: Utopian Family — Alternatives to the Traditional Family Model
Host: host-zara
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-15
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

In this discussion group we will examine the most basic unit of human collectivity beyond the individual. How do we organize intimate interdependence? What can alternative kinship structures teach us about care, resource-sharing, and decision-making at small scales? The family is often the laboratory for collective practices.

Key optional readings:

### Topic: topic-zero-knowledge-proofs

Title: Zero-Knowledge Proofs
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

In a zero-knowledge proof, a prover aims to convince a verifier of the truth of some statement (e.g., that they know a password) without revealing anything beyond that it is true. This turns out to be a powerful primitive, with applications to voting systems, machine learning, cryptocurrencies, and many other areas! I have spent my whole career working on zero knowledge and would be happy to discuss zero-knowledge proofs at any level: how to build them, what guarantees they do and don't provide, whether or not they could (or should) be used for a given application, etc.

### Topic: topic-cryptographic-transparency

Title: Cryptographic Transparency
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

There are defined cryptographic notions of transparency, and there are cryptographic primitives that get used to build systems that provide strong transparency guarantees. There are also successfully deployed technical projects like Certificate Transparency (which all major browsers use every time you visit a website), key transparency (deployed in WhatsApp), and software transparency (Sigstore). While transparency thus can be a necessary tool for achieving fairness and accountability in complex multi-party systems, it is far from sufficient, both for these more technological systems but especially for more human-oriented systems (e.g., using transparency for governance, as in a DAO).

### Topic: topic-online-security-and-privacy

Title: Online Security and Privacy
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

There is universal security advice that applies to anyone who is online (e.g., using strong passwords and two-factor authentication), and specific security advice that applies to those who are at elevated risk of being targeted online in some way (which includes almost everyone, at some point in their lives). Beyond that, there are many ways in which we may choose to maintain an online presence. It's valuable to understand the risks that we or those we work with may face and how those risks might change over time (sometimes gradually and sometimes quickly; for example if someone joins a political campaign), and to think through both reasonable precautions to prevent these attacks and how to react when they do happen.

### Topic: topic-online-help-seeking

Title: Online Help Seeking for Digital Privacy, Safety, and Security
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

People seek help online constantly, for a variety of reasons and from a variety of sources: search engines, social media, online fora, LLMs, etc. Some of my recent research has looked at how people seek advice around their digital privacy, safety, and security, both in terms of the questions they ask (and how they ask them) and the quality of advice they get from different sources. This allows us to understand the wide range of problems people face; e.g., scams, harassment, issues accessing accounts or using security- or privacy-focused tools (VPNs, antivirus, ad blockers, etc.), malware, and more.

### Topic: topic-software-supply-chains

Title: Software Supply Chains
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Modern software is developed in a collaborative way, with developers choosing to use code from multiple third-party libraries rather than implement everything from scratch. This interdependent software supply chain has benefits for security, but it also comes with risks in the form of supply-chain attacks, such as the highly publicized attack on SolarWinds or the Log4Shell vulnerability. I have done some research looking at software supply chains, both in terms of examining dependencies in open-source software and their impact on security and in terms of exploring how the same principles and protections can extend to machine learning models.

### Topic: topic-cryptography-threat-modeling

Title: Cryptography / Threat Modeling
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

In addition to the specific topics highlighted above, I'd be happy to chat about any cryptographic primitives (signatures, encryption, multi-party computation, voting, etc.) and/or go through a project or setting you have in mind and talk about threat models.

### Topic: topic-security-and-privacy-in-ml

Title: Security and Privacy in Machine Learning
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I don't have as much expertise in this topic as the other ones listed, but I follow the research on adversarial machine learning reasonably closely, and have published on things like machine learning supply chains, auditing ML models without access to the training data (using zero knowledge!), and how well models can reason about information sharing.

### Topic: topic-programming-sarah

Title: Programming
Host: host-sadie
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-16
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I enjoy coding, both for personal projects and for research, where most of my coding involves data science-type tasks in Python. If one of your goals for this year is to learn to code then I'd be happy to support that! I am not the right person to ask about vibecoding, or getting a specific project done, but if you want to learn how to program in Python in a principled way then I have materials available from teaching this (to non-technical students) in the past.

### Topic: topic-open-social-web

Title: Open Social Web (ATProto and ActivityPub)
Host: host-anya
Status: submitted
Published date, if published:
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Bluesky and Mastodon are emergent microblogging platforms designed to reduce the centralisation of power in the social media ecosystem. Bluesky especially is notable due to its large userbase and wide adoption by the world's media. This topic will discuss similarities and differences between these two technologies, as well as those between decentralised and traditional social media. Opportunities for innovation and expansion within these spaces will also be discussed.

I run the bimonthly atproto.london meetup here at Newspeak House as well as co-host Journalism Technology London, also at Newspeak. If you want to build something cool in the ATProto space, I can absolutely help you with that!

### Topic: topic-visual-information-design

Title: Visual Information Design
Host: host-anya
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-17
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Visual design is increasingly a major part of how we understand the world, with data visualisation being a primary lens through which the general public understands the myriad data produced by governments and organisations. In this topic I'll discuss basic principles of visual design in relation to data visualisation, what pitfalls to avoid, and why we all have a shared responsibility to visualise data honestly and accurately.

### Topic: topic-how-do-media-organisations-work

Title: How Do Media Organisations Work?
Host: host-anya
Status: archived
Published date, if published: 2026-05-02
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I've worked in traditional media organisations my entire career and they're weird places. Understanding the economics of the industry (as well as the motivations of the people working in it) is helpful for illuminating why the media does what it does. This topic will use moral panics in the UK as a lens through which to view historical behaviours of the press from the 1950s to present day.

### Topic: topic-telling-stories-with-data

Title: Telling Stories with Data
Host: host-anya
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-17
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Get started with data journalism by interrogating datasets and using Freedom Of Information (FOI) requests to investigate public bodies. I'll walk you through filing your first FOI via WhatDoTheyKnow.com, how to search data.gov.uk, and what to do when you finally get that data loaded into a spreadsheet application.

### Topic: topic-politics-of-social-media

Title: The Politics of Social Media
Host: host-anya
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-17
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

We are living through a tumultuous time for the world's information ecosystem, and nowhere is this more apparent than in the social media space. Between platforms being weaponised by reactionary forces and the resulting legislative blowback from governmental bodies, social media has never before been so politicised. Nowhere is this more evident than in the decentralised microblogging space, with Bluesky and other networks subject to everything from age verification laws to thinly-veiled threats by American conservative politicians. Yet, perhaps decentralisation is a route by which we can start building a better social media, one that is more user-centric and prioritises social needs over the profit of large corporations. In this topic we will analyse Blacksky, Eurosky and Northsky as alternative futures for social media, and why data sovereignty is increasingly important for how we structure these information webs.

### Topic: topic-moderation-and-social-media

Title: Moderation and Social Media
Host: host-anya
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-17
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Moderation is more than the sum of the decisions made by community management teams on social media platforms — it is ultimately the social contract that upholds norms within online spaces, and with that comes a great degree of power to define goals and borders of those spaces. In a sense, moderation is the politics of the online domain. This topic will discuss multiple approaches to moderation, including Bluesky's composable moderation via 3rd party labellers, and the Fediverse's approach of independently moderated islands that are part of a decentralised ecosystem.

<!-- ===================== Host: Aaron Vance ===================== -->

### Topic: topic-how-governance-works-in-britain

Title: How Governance Actually Works in Britain
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of people understand Britain's political system formally but not operationally. They know about Parliament, Ministers, departments, regulators, local government and the Civil Service, but not how decisions actually move between them.

I can help fellows understand the difference between constitutional power, administrative power, political attention and practical leverage. That includes questions like: Who actually decides? Who can block? Who implements? Who carries risk? What happens when formal authority and operational reality point in different directions? This is especially useful for fellows interested in public institutions, reform, state capacity, democratic systems, civic technology or policy entrepreneurship.

### Topic: topic-strategy-getting-big-things-done

Title: Strategy and Getting Big Things Done
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Most ambitious projects fail not because the idea is bad, but because the strategy is vague. "Raise awareness", "influence government" and "build a movement" are not strategies by themselves. They need to become choices about actors, incentives, sequencing, legitimacy, pressure, trade-offs and timing.

I can help fellows move from a broad ambition to a practical route to change. That might include actor mapping, identifying veto points, choosing insider versus outsider tactics, designing escalation ladders, building coalitions, or deciding when a quiet conversation is more useful than a public campaign. I'm particularly interested in helping people understand influence without fantasy. Power is not always where it appears to be, and access is not the same thing as leverage.

### Topic: topic-serious-games

Title: Serious Games as Tools for Learning and Strategy
Host: host-aaron
Status: submitted
Published date, if published:
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Serious games are not just "fun workshops". Used well, they are tools for thinking. They let people inhabit incentives, test assumptions, reveal hidden constraints and understand systems that are too complex to explain in a slide deck.

I can help fellows design games about politics, governance, crisis, public administration, contracts, conflict, institutions and social systems. That includes thinking through objectives, player roles, mechanics, incentives, adjudication, escalation, information flows and learning outcomes. I'm particularly interested in games where the lesson emerges from play rather than being preached at the players. A good serious game should make people feel the problem in their hands.

### Topic: topic-state-capacity-institutional-failure

Title: State Capacity and Institutional Failure
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of the most important political questions eventually become delivery questions. Can the state actually do the thing? Does it have the data, capability, authority, money, trust and operational grip? What happens when responsibility is fragmented across departments, contractors, regulators and delivery bodies?

I can help fellows think about public-sector failure in practical terms: incentives, governance, accountability, data ownership, delivery chains, outsourcing, crisis recovery and the gap between policy intent and operational reality. This is useful for anyone interested in reform, public services, infrastructure, procurement, digital government or the practical limits of "just make government do X".

### Topic: topic-legitimacy-authority-consent

Title: Legitimacy, Authority and Consent
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Many institutional problems are not really persuasion problems. They are legitimacy problems. People may agree something needs to change but disagree about who has the right to decide, whether the process is fair, whether the evidence is trusted, or whether the people leading the work understand the consequences.

I can help fellows think about how legitimacy is built in practice: through participation, transparency, competence, sequencing, evidence, consultation, ownership and visible fairness. This matters in government, but also in communities, movements, organisations, civic projects and any environment where formal authority is weak or contested.

### Topic: topic-crisis-escalation-decision-making

Title: Crisis, Escalation and Decision-Making Under Pressure
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Institutions behave differently in a crisis. Attention narrows, risk appetite changes, people bypass normal process, and short-term fixes can create long-term vulnerability. A lot of strategy is understanding how to act under pressure without destroying your position later.

I can help fellows think through crisis dynamics: escalation, accountability, political attention, operational grip, communications, trade-offs, and the point at which stabilising the system starts to undermine future leverage. This is an area where serious games are particularly valuable, because they let people practise pressure before the real crisis arrives.

### Topic: topic-designing-civic-interventions

Title: Designing Civic and Institutional Interventions
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

A lot of civic projects fail because they solve an imagined problem rather than a real one. The hard bit is not only having a good idea, but understanding the user, the workflow, the institution, the adoption barrier and the incentive structure.

I can help fellows move from idea to intervention: What problem are you actually solving? Who needs to change behaviour? What would make adoption rational? What evidence would convince people? What existing process does this need to fit inside? When should you build something new, and when should you adapt what already exists? I'm especially interested in practical interventions that increase agency, competence, coordination and trust.

### Topic: topic-leadership-convening-stewardship

Title: Leadership, Convening and Institutional Stewardship
Host: host-aaron
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-18
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Some kinds of power come from formal authority. Others come from convening, sense-making and helping groups act together. In complex systems, the ability to bring the right people into the right conversation at the right moment can be decisive.

I can help fellows think about leadership as stewardship: creating the conditions for good people to do more good, building trust across boundaries, clarifying choices, and helping groups move without pretending conflict does not exist. This includes practical questions like: How do you design a useful meeting? How do you build a network that actually does something? How do you help senior people make better decisions? How do you create enough shared understanding for action?

### Topic: topic-the-nature-of-voting

Title: The Nature of Voting
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

This conversation is aimed at faculty. Standard ideas about what voting is, how it operates, and where it comes from are a set of widely held assumptions that are rarely challenged. These assumptions are often present in the foundations of political, democracy, and participation projects.

By researching the evolution of voting from animal herd behaviors, through ancient history, and into the present day, I can offer a different description of what is going on when this protocol of counting is used.

If you're trying to answer questions like: How are people influenced in their voting? What are the optimal features of a fair collective decision system? What voting system is appropriate for what kinds of questions, then this conversation will help you start from the beginning.

Reference: *The Majority Myth*, Eli Morgan.

### Topic: topic-demography-voting-and-numbers

Title: Demography, Voting, and Numbers
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

What can be said about the different numbers and quantities used in voting systems? Is voting scalable — does it work the same way for 60 people as for 60 million? What is implied by the numbers used in juries, panels of judges, etc.? What is the precise meaning of the threshold for winning an election?

This session is of interest to those who are suspicious of the maths used in elections, democracy, and discourse. We will take some time to debunk assumptions about majorities that frequently pop up in internet arguments, but we will also look at the aristocracy of voting intellectuals and academia: Kenneth Arrow, Amartya Sen, Rousseau and others, and see whether their assumptions about the meaning of different vote counts hold water.

Reference: Sen, Amartya (1970). *Collective Choice and Social Welfare*. Edinburgh: Oliver & Boyd.

### Topic: topic-audience-participation

Title: Audience Participation
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

TV votes are everywhere. What can the ways that entertainment uses voting teach us about how engagement with large numbers of people happens? From Big Brother to Britain's Got Talent, audience participation has become a mainstay of TV shows. We will break down these systems and think aloud about what they are good at.

### Topic: topic-arhuaco-philosophy

Title: Arhuaco Philosophy and its Relevance
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Ignorance of native American political ideas is a generalized feature of western and eastern political thinking. The Arhuaco Tribe of Colombia have resisted colonization, both physical and intellectual, until the present day — a story which counts as a miracle of resilience. The tribe has institutions and traditions of deliberation, dialogue, and decision-making which are independent of enlightenment western norms, making it a fascinating and rare glimpse of diversity in decision making collectives. Over the past 10 years I have had the privilege of researching, interviewing and living with Arhuaco leaders and the wider community. In this session we will ask questions directly to some Arhuaco people.

### Topic: topic-metaphors-of-the-collective

Title: Metaphors of the Collective
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

What are the different ways in which the collectives and political activities you work with are imagined? Getting clear about what metaphor is in play can help us stay honest when it comes to generalizations.

The leviathan is some kind of beast. Elections are a sporting 'race'. Elections either work or do not work. Rhetoric is divisive and poisonous.

### Topic: topic-designing-rituals-of-participation

Title: Designing Rituals of Participation
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Many of you know that the central thesis of my book *The Majority Myth* is that voting is usually a social ritual. If that is at all true, then those of us who wish to foster or impulse collective decision of any kind ought to be in the business of ritual design. Just as a wedding planner has to consider every aspect of the wedding ceremony, from the material used on the chairs to what people see when they enter the room, so a decision ritual designer takes the view that the process taking place is one of changing the participants' minds. That means that even for online voting, the colour and shape and feedback animation of every button is of interest and contributes to the overall collective decision.

The Collective Dynamics Lab is largely focused on this enterprise. I will look with a limited group at their particular collective participation 'systems' through the lens of this approach, and we will design and then vibe code some possible solutions.

### Topic: topic-herds-birds-and-words

Title: Herds, Birds, and Words
Host: host-eli
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-08
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

An exploration of animal collective decision methods, what they are based upon, and how they relate to human decision protocols historically and in the present day.

### Topic: topic-data-visualisation-nash

Title: Data Visualisation
Host: host-jordan
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-20
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I've built mapping platforms, public opinion tools and open-data projects over the years, and I'm interested in how information can be presented in ways that genuinely improve understanding. I'm particularly influenced by the work of Edward Tufte and the broader field of information design. I can help fellows think about questions like: What is the most effective way to communicate a complex idea? How do you reveal patterns, relationships and uncertainty? When should information be visualised, and when shouldn't it? I'm also interested in how AI-powered coding and analysis tools are changing what's possible, making sophisticated visualisation techniques faster and easier.

### Topic: topic-complex-adaptive-systems

Title: Complex Adaptive Systems and Democratic Design
Host: host-jordan
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-20
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

While leading the Combined Choice project at Demos, I spent a great deal of time thinking about the mechanics of democratic decision-making and how democratic systems might be improved. I can help fellows think through questions about incentives, coordination, feedback loops and institutional design. Why do some systems consistently produce good outcomes while others fail? How do markets, ecosystems and other complex adaptive systems organise themselves? What lessons can democratic institutions learn from them? Much of my work focuses on thinking from first principles about how systems work, where power sits, and how outcomes emerge from the interactions between people, rules and incentives.

### Topic: topic-the-basics-of-polling

Title: The Basics of Polling
Host: host-jordan
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-20
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

I've worked in and founded opinion research companies and have spent years thinking about how public opinion is measured and understood. I can help fellows understand where polling and opinion research can be useful, how to design good questions, how to interpret results, and how to avoid common mistakes. I'm particularly interested in helping people think critically about research: what it can tell us, what it can't tell us, and how evidence should be used in decision-making.

### Topic: topic-low-hanging-fruit

Title: Low-Hanging Fruit
Host: host-jordan
Status: published
Published date, if published: 2026-06-20
Cover image URL, if any:

Body:

Many of the best opportunities are overlooked because they appear too simple, unfashionable or unglamorous. I can help fellows identify opportunities where relatively small technological interventions could create outsized social impact. This includes thinking about questions like: What problems are everyone ignoring? Why have certain opportunities been overlooked? Which ideas are genuinely promising, and which are likely to become "tar pit" projects that consume enormous effort without delivering results? I'm particularly interested in combining first-principles thinking, research and modern AI tools to identify opportunities that are both impactful and achievable.

## Notes for engineers

- **Statuses cover all five states**: published (most), draft (title-only / placeholder
  topics), submitted (topic-reform, topic-open-social-web, topic-serious-games),
  unpublished (topic-software-development, topic-getting-funded), archived
  (topic-how-do-media-organisations-work). Adjust freely.
- **Placeholder bodies**: topics that were lorem-ipsum in the source are marked
  `_Draft — body to be written._` rather than filled with filler text. Say the word and
  I'll generate realistic blurbs for these so every topic renders with real content.
- **Harvey / Zara split**: the source doc had a duplicate host heading. The first set
  (web data, structured extraction, local AI, data pipelines) is Harvey Dunmore's; the
  second (collective-intelligence / utopias series) is Zara Ashworth's (host-zara).
- **Names are fictional**: all display names are anonymised placeholders (initials
  preserved), so the file is safe to commit to the public repo as-is.
- **No emails** are included. Add fake ones only if the seed script needs them.
- **Hosts as electors**: `host-eli` holds both `host` and `elector` roles, enabling dual-role UX testing (weighted hearts from a host, host-only comment access, etc.).
- **Custom role labels** (Dean / Faculty / Fellow) come from the spec's suggestion that
  timetables can rename roles; drop them if v1 doesn't support custom labels yet.
- **Cover images**: `topic-cryptocurrencies` and `topic-ai` have cover image URLs set via picsum.photos with stable seeds.
- **Submitted with feedback**: `topic-serious-games` is submitted and has a host-only admin comment (`c-games-1`), which surfaces as the `feedback` field in the moderation queue and host topic manager.
- **Not yet modelled** (tracked in issue #44): timeslots / sessions, elector availability, slot discussions, slot-topic tags, and the resulting conflict alerts on the dashboard.
